\"GCC's RTL (Register Transfer Language) passes are organized through a class hierarchy defined in gcc/tree-pass.h. The base class is opt_pass, from which rtl_opt_pass extends as a specialization for RTL-level transformations. Each pass has associated metadata in a pass_data structure that defines the pass type, name, properties, and timing information.\\n\\nThe RTL pass chain begins with pass_expand (gcc/cfgexpand.cc:7010), which implements the critical gimple-to-RTL conversion. The pass_expand class inherits from rtl_opt_pass and implements the execute() method that performs the initial expansion from GIMPLE intermediate representation to RTL form, handling basic blocks, control flow, and statement expansion.\\n\\nA representative RTL optimization pass is pass_combine (gcc/combine.cc:15268), which performs instruction combining to reduce RTL instruction sequences. It demonstrates the typical structure of RTL passes: inheriting from rtl_opt_pass, implementing a gate() method for optimization control, and an execute() method that calls rest_of_handle_combine() to perform the actual optimization work.\\n\\nAnother important RTL optimization pass is pass_ira (gcc/ira.cc:6205), which performs integrated register allocation and movement optimization. This pass uses IRA (Integrated Register Allocator) to assign hardware registers to virtual registers and optimize register pressure throughout the function.\\n\\nThe final code generation pass is pass_final (gcc/final.cc:4340), which generates the final assembly output. This pass calls rest_of_handle_final() which orchestrates the final processing steps: assembling function prologue, emitting RTL instructions as assembly, handling exception tables, and assembling the function epilogue. It outputs the target architecture's assembly instructions through the ASM output file.\\n\\nThe RTL pass chain is orchestrated through passes.def (gcc/passes.def), which uses NEXT_PASS macros to define the order of execution. Key passes execute in sequence: after pass_expand generates RTL, optimization passes like pass_combine improve the RTL, register allocation passes like pass_ira assign registers, and finally pass_final generates the target assembly code. This pipeline transforms high-level GIMPLE code through increasingly low-level representations until producing executable machine code.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2618,"cache_read_input_tokens":73836,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2618},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"d9816da8-f647-426f-8ea5-5eff7587564e","uuid":"eb92e26b-54a9-4e42-80b3-00d9dfa81c1b"}

It demonstrates the typical structure of RTL passes: inheriting from rtl_opt_pass, implementing a gate() method for optimization control, and an execute() method that calls rest_of_handle_combine() to perform the actual optimization work.\\n\\nAnother important RTL optimization pass is pass_ira (gcc/ira.cc:6205), which performs integrated register allocation and movement optimization. This pass uses IRA (Integrated Register Allocator) to assign hardware registers to virtual registers and optimize register pressure throughout the function.\\n\\nThe final code generation pass is pass_final (gcc/final.cc:4340), which generates the final assembly output. This pass calls rest_of_handle_final() which orchestrates the final processing steps: assembling function prologue, emitting RTL instructions as assembly, handling exception tables, and assembling the function epilogue. It outputs the target architecture's assembly instructions through the ASM output file.\\n\\nThe RTL pass chain is orchestrated through passes.def (gcc/passes.def), which uses NEXT_PASS macros to define the order of execution. Key passes execute in sequence: after pass_expand generates RTL, optimization passes like pass_combine improve the RTL, register allocation passes like pass_ira assign registers, and finally pass_final generates the target assembly code. This pipeline transforms high-level GIMPLE code through increasingly low-level representations until producing executable machine code.\"\n    88→}\n    89→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware.
